Two Slaves Fighting: Mutual Aggression and Liability
Rulings on two slaves fighting and various death/injury outcomes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for two slaves fighting and apply the rule of badal (substitute compensation) to determine master's liability in various injury and death outcomes.

Core Idea
When two slaves fight and survive, masters exchange slaves; each receives a complete substitute, so no further claim remains.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explores intricate liability rules when two slaves engage in mutual aggression. The central concept is badal: the substituted compensation. The master's choice between handing over the slave or paying compensation ensures justice in overlapping injuries. We will walk through the baseline scenario and its variations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the baseline scenario
Two slaves meet, each with a stick. They fight and both survive. What is the default ruling? Each master gives his slave to the other, and neither can reclaim anything because each now owns a complete slave in substitution.
This is the foundational rule: the badal (substitute) is the other slave.
2
Understand the principle of badal
The 'badal' is the substitute given in compensation. Here, it is the slave himself, not money. The right of each master attaches to a complete sound slave, so exchanging is the default.
If one master chooses ransom (fida), he must pay the full value of his slave's injury.
3
Trace the master's choice
The master may choose to hand over the slave or pay compensation (ransom). When both fight, both masters have the same choices. But if one struck first (initiator), his master has the choice; the other master also has choice, but with different consequences.
The initiator's master is given choice, not the later master's master.
4
Distinguish initiator vs. later
If one slave strikes first, the master of the initiator is given choice (to hand over or ransom). The master of the later slave then has a choice only if the initiator's master ransoms. This prevents circular claims.
The later's right is in a complete sound slave, so he can reclaim if the initiator's slave is injured.
5
Apply to death scenarios
If the initiator dies, his value is on the neck of the later slave; the later's master can either pay the value or ransom. If the killer dies, the initiator's master has choice. Each scenario ensures that the right of each master is satisfied without double compensation.
The principle of badal continues: the dead slave is replaced by his value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عبدان التقيا ومع كل واحد عصا فاضطربا وبرئا دفع مولى كل واحد بالآخر ولا يرجعان بشيء سوى لأن كل واحد منهما ملك عبده من صاحبه ولا يفيد التراجع لأنه لو رجع أحدهما لرجع الآخر لأن حق كل واحد منهما ثبت في رقبة كاملة، فما يأخذ أحدهما من صاحبه فذاك بدل آخر وتعلق به حقه فلا يفيد الرجوع وإن اختار الفداء فدى كل واحد بجميع أرش جنايته لأنهما لما اضطربا معاً فقد جنى كل واحد منهما على عبد فتعلق حق كل واحد من الموليين بعبد صحيح فيجب بدل عبد صحيح، وإن سبق أحدهما بالضربة خير مولى البادئ لأن البداية من مولى اللاحق لا تفيد لأن حق اللاحق في عبد صحيح كامل الرقبة، فإذا دفع إلى البادئ عبده مشجوجاً كان للاحق أن يسترده منه فكان دفعه مفيداً، فإن دفعه فالعبد للمدفوع إليه ولا شيء للدافع لأنه لو رجع البادئ بشيء كان للمدفوع إليه أن . يرجع عليه ثانياً لأن حقه في رقبة عبد صحيح فلا يفيد رجوع البادئ، وإن فداه خير مولى اللاحق بين البدفع والفداء لأنه برئ عبد البادئ عن الجناية بالفداء وصار كأنه لم يجن وإن جنى عليه العبد اللاحق فإن مات البادئ كانت قيمته في عنق الثاني يدفع بها أو يفدي، فإن فداه بقيمة الميت يرجع في تلك القيمة بأرش جراحة عبد وصار كأنه لم يجن، وإنما جنى عليه البادئ والبادئ إن مات فالقيمة قائمة مقامه لأنه قائم وإن دفعه بأرش شجة عبده في عنقه ويخير المدفوع إليه بين الدفع والفداء لأن المدفوع قام مقام الميت الشاج. وإن مات العبد القاتل خير مولى العبد الباديء، فإن فداه أو دفع بطل حقه في شجته حين شج اللاحق البادئ كان اللاحق مشجوجاً فثبت حق المولى البادئ في شجة عبده . ولو مات البادئ من شيء آخر سوى الجناية وبقي اللاحق خير المولى ويقال له إذا شئت ادفع واعف عن مولى اللاحق ولا سبيل لواحد منهما على الآخر، وإن شئت ادفع أرش شجة اللاحق وطالبه، فإن دفع إلى صاحبه أرش عبده يرجع بأرش جناية عبده فيدفع مولى اللاحق عبده أو يفده ؛ أما العفو فلأنه مولى البادئ بجنايته وإذا دفع كان لمولى اللاحق أن يطالبه بأرش شجة عبده وكان لمولى البادئ أن يدفع إليه العبد المدفوع ثانياً ليبرأ عن حقه فلا يفيد الدفع. وإنما دفع أرش شجة اللاحق لأنه متى دفع أرش عبد اللاحق فقد طهر البادئ عن الجناية وصار كأنه لم يجن، وإنما جنى عليه العبد اللاحق فيخاطب مولى اللاحق بالدفع أو الفداء وأي ذلك اختار لا يبقى لواحد منهما على صاحبه سبيل لأنه وصل إلى كل واحد منهما حقه، وإن أبى مولى البادئ أن يدفع الأرش فلا تعلق له في عنق الحر لأن مولى البادئ كان مخيراً بين العفو وبين دفع الأرش والمطالبة بشجة عبده، فإذا امتنع من دفع الأرش صار مختاراً للعفو وصار كأنه قال عفوتك عن حق فبطل حقه. ولو مات اللاحق وبقي البادئ خير مولاه. فإن دفعه بطل حقه، وإن فداه بأرش فداه عبده وفي الفداء لأن البادئ طهر عن جنايته.
Two slaves met, each with a stick, they fought and were cured (survived). The master of each gives (his slave) to the other, and they do not take back anything because each of them owns his slave from the other, and returning is not beneficial because if one returns, the other returns, because the right of each is established in a complete slave. So what one takes from the other is an alternate substitute and his right is attached to it, so returning is not beneficial. If he chooses ransom, each ransoms with the full compensation of his injury because when they fought together, each injured a slave, so the right of each master is attached to a sound slave, so the compensation of a sound slave is obligatory. If one preceded in striking, the master of the initiator is given choice because the initiation from the master of the later does not benefit, because the right of the later is in a complete sound slave. So if he gives to the initiator his slave injured, the later has the right to take it back from him, so his giving was beneficial. If he gives, the slave is for the recipient and nothing for the giver because if the initiator returns something, the recipient would return again because his right is in the complete slave, so the initiator's return is not beneficial. If he ransoms, the master of the later is given choice between giving and ransoming because the initiator's slave becomes free of injury by ransom, as if he did not injure, even if the later slave injured him. If the initiator dies, his value is on the neck of the later; he gives it or ransoms. If he ransoms with the value of the dead, he recovers from that value the compensation of his slave's wound, as if he did not injure, but the initiator injured him, and if the initiator dies, the value stands in his place because he is standing. If he gives with the compensation of his slave's wound on his neck, the recipient is given choice between giving and ransoming because the recipient stands in place of the dead injurer. If the killer slave dies, the master of the initiator slave is given choice. If he ransoms or gives, his right in his wound is void when the later injured the initiator, the later was injured, so the master of the initiator's right in his slave's wound is established. And if the initiator dies from something other than the injury and the later remains, the master is given choice and it is said to him: if you wish, give and forgive the master of the later, and no way for one upon the other; if you wish, give the compensation of the later's wound and claim it. If he gives to his companion the compensation of his slave, he recovers with the compensation of his slave's injury, then the master of the later gives his slave or ransoms him. As for forgiveness, because he is the master of the initiator due to his injury, and if he gives, the master of the later can claim the compensation of his slave's wound, and the master of the initiator can give the given slave again to free himself from his right, so giving is not beneficial. He only gives the compensation of the later's wound because when he gives the compensation of the later's slave, he cleanses the initiator from the injury, as if he did not injure, and only the later slave injured him. Then the master of the later is addressed with giving or ransoming, and whichever he chooses, no way remains for one upon the other because each reached his right. If the master of the initiator refuses to give the compensation, there is no claim on the free man because the master of the initiator was given choice between forgiveness and giving compensation and claiming his slave's wound. When he refrained from giving compensation, he became a chooser of forgiveness, as if he said: 'I forgive you for the right,' so his right is void. And if the later dies and the initiator remains, his master is given choice. If he gives, his right is void; if he ransoms with compensation, he ransoms his slave, because the initiator is cleansed from his injury.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings regarding two slaves who engage in a mutual fight. The key principles: when both survive, each master must exchange his slave with the other, and no further recourse because each receives a complete slave in compensation. If one chooses to pay blood-money instead, he pays the full value of the injury. If one strikes first (the initiator), his master has the choice to hand over the slave or pay; the later (victim) master has the choice. Various scenarios of death or injury are detailed, always ensuring that the liability is shifted appropriately. The master of the initiator can choose to pay compensation to the later's master and then claim his own compensation. Ultimately, if the initiator's master refuses to pay, his claim is voided, analogized to forgiveness. These rulings demonstrate the Hanafi approach to overlapping liabilities in slave injuries.

Key Terms
بدل (badal): Substitute compensation; the slave given or value paid in exchange for the injury.
فداء (fida): Ransom; paying compensation to release the slave from liability.
خير (khayar): Choice; the master is given the option to either hand over the slave or pay compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case of two slaves fighting and both survive, what is the default ruling for their masters?
A) Each master pays half the value of his slave to the other.
B) Each master gives his slave to the other, and no return is allowed.
C) The initiator's master must pay full compensation, and the other receives nothing.
D) Both slaves are set free as penalty.

Key Takeaway
When two slaves fight, the default compensation is the exchange of slaves; the master's choice to ransom or exchange ensures each receives a complete substitute without circular claims.

Ruling on Two Slaves Fighting and Both Dying
Explains ruling when two slaves fight and both die, with master's options

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two slaves fight and die, explain the master's options (exchange or ransom), and justify why no recourse is permitted.

Core Idea
When two slaves kill each other, each master compensates with his slave or pays full value — no right of recourse.

This passage from al-Muhit addresses a specific scenario of mutual homicide between slaves. Understanding the ruling requires grasping the principle that each master's right attaches to a sound slave, leading to an exchange with no recourse. The master may also choose to pay the full arsh instead.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Two slaves, each armed with a stick, strike each other and both die. The ruling: each master must compensate the other for the loss of his slave.
The compensation is wajib (obligatory) because the slave is property.
2
Understand the Master's Two Options
The master may either hand over his own slave to the other master (exchange) or pay the full arsh (compensation for the injury) as ransom (fidya). The choice is the master's.
If exchange is chosen, each master becomes owner of the other's slave.
3
Grasp the Reasoning for No Recourse
After exchange, each master owns a complete slave. Any attempt to take back compensation would be met by a similar claim from the other, leading to a circular deadlock. Thus, recourse is not beneficial.
The right of each master is attached to a complete neck.
4
Recognize the Full Arsh Rationale for Ransom
If the master chooses ransom, he must pay the full arsh because his slave injured a sound slave of the other. Since both injuries occurred simultaneously, the full value is due.
The arsh is the amount by which the slave's value is diminished.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
دية كل واحد منهما نصف الدية أو دفع نصف العبد لهما فيخير المولى بينهما؛ كذا ذكر الشارح . قال في المحيط : :: عبدان التقيا ومع كل واحد عصا فاضطربا وبرئا دفع مولى كل واحد بالآخر ولا يرجعان بشيء سوى لأن كل واحد منهما ملك عبده من صاحبه ولا يفيد التراجع لأنه لو رجع أحدهما لرجع الآخر لأن حق كل واحد منهما ثبت في رقبة كاملة، فما يأخذ أحدهما من صاحبه فذاك بدل آخر وتعلق به حقه فلا يفيد الرجوع وإن اختار الفداء فدى كل واحد بجميع أرش جنايته لأنهما لما اضطربا معاً فقد جنى كل واحد منهما على عبد فتعلق حق كل واحد من الموليين بعبد صحيح فيجب بدل عبد صحيح،
The blood money of each of them is half the blood money or payment of half of the slave to both, so the master chooses between them; thus stated the commentator. He said in al-Muhit: Two slaves met, each with a stick, they struck each other and died. The master of each pays the other slave (as compensation) and they do not have recourse for anything, because each of them owns the slave of the other, and recourse is not beneficial because if one had recourse, the other would also have recourse, since the right of each is established in a complete neck. So what one takes from the other is another substitute and his right is attached to it, so recourse is not beneficial. If he chooses ransom, each ransoms with the full compensation of his injury, because when they struck together, each injured a slave, so the right of each master is attached to a sound slave, so the substitute of a sound slave is obligatory.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the Hanafi school concerning two slaves who fight and both die from the injuries. The author quotes from al-Muhit. The ruling: Each master is entitled to either half the full blood money (diyah) of a slave or the payment of half a slave to each, and the master chooses which option. In the scenario where both die, the master of each gives the other slave as compensation (i.e., they exchange slaves) and neither has recourse to take anything back from the other. The reasoning is that each master now owns the other's slave completely, so any attempt at recourse would be countered by the other's similar right. If a master chooses ransom (fidya), he pays the full compensation (arsh) for the injury caused by his slave. Since they both struck simultaneously, each injured the other's slave, so each master's right is attached to a sound slave, thus the full value is due.

Key Terms
دية (diyah): Blood money, compensation paid for homicide or injury.
أرش (arsh): Compensation for injury, the amount by which the value of the slave is diminished.
عبد (abd): Slave, in this context a male slave.
مولى (mawla): Master, owner of the slave.
فداء (fida): Ransom, the option to pay cash compensation instead of handing over the slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When two slaves fight and both die, what is the default compensation option (if the master does not choose ransom)?
A) Each master pays half diyah to the other.
B) Each master gives his own slave to the other.
C) The first striker's master pays full diyah.
D) The masters share the combined diyah equally.

Key Takeaway
When two slaves kill each other, the masters exchange slaves or pay full arsh, with no right of subsequent recourse.

Ruling When One Slave Strikes First
Explains ruling when one slave strikes first, with master's options.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when one slave strikes first and the other retaliates, and explain the options available to each master.

Core Idea
The master of the first striker has a choice; the later striker's master is entitled to a sound slave.

When two slaves fight and one strikes first, the subsequent legal relationships between their masters are governed by a key principle: the later striker's master has a right to a sound, complete slave. This lesson unpacks the options available to each master based on the text from Al-Bahr al-Raiq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Recognize the roles: the first striker (البادئ) and the later striker (اللاحق). Note that the text focuses on the rights of the later striker's master.
The later striker's master is the one who suffered injury to his slave.
2
Understand the initial choice
The master of the first striker is given a choice (تخيير) between handing over his wounded slave or ransoming him. However, this choice is conditioned by the later striker's right to a sound slave.
The initiation of the later striker's master is not beneficial because his right is to a sound slave.
3
Analyze the effect of handing over the slave
If the first striker's master pays his wounded slave, the later striker's master can reject it and take back the slave, since the slave is not whole. The payment is only beneficial if it leads to resolution.
The later striker's master retains the right to a sound slave.
4
Consider the case of the first striker's death
If the first striker dies, his value is owed by the later striker's master. The later striker's master can either pay the value or ransom, and may later claim compensation for the wound.
The value stands in place of the deceased slave.
5
Summarize the takhyir structure
Both masters have options that are interlinked. The first striker's master chooses payment or ransom; the second's master can then choose to accept or demand a sound slave. This ensures fairness.
The ruling prevents the later striker's master from being disadvantaged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن سبق أحدهما بالضربة خير مولى البادئ لأن البداية من مولى اللاحق لا تفيد لأن حق اللاحق في عبد صحيح كامل الرقبة، فإذا دفع إلى البادئ عبده مشجوجاً كان للاحق أن يسترده منه فكان دفعه مفيداً، فإن دفعه فالعبد للمدفوع إليه ولا شيء للدافع لأنه لو رجع البادئ بشيء كان للمدفوع إليه أن . يرجع عليه ثانياً لأن حقه في رقبة عبد صحيح فلا يفيد رجوع البادئ، وإن فداه خير مولى اللاحق بين البدفع والفداء لأنه برئ عبد البادئ عن الجناية بالفداء وصار كأنه لم يجن وإن جنى عليه العبد اللاحق فإن مات البادئ كانت قيمته في عنق الثاني يدفع بها أو يفدي، فإن فداه بقيمة الميت يرجع في تلك القيمة بأرش جراحة عبد وصار كأنه لم يجن، وإنما جنى عليه البادئ والبادئ إن مات فالقيمة قائمة مقامه لأنه قائم وإن دفعه بأرش شجة عبده في عنقه ويخير المدفوع إليه بين الدفع والفداء لأن المدفوع قام مقام الميت الشاج.
And if one of them strikes first, the master of the first striker is given a choice because the initiation from the master of the later striker is not beneficial, because the right of the later striker is in a sound complete slave. So if he pays to the first striker his slave with a wound, the later striker has the right to take it back from him, so his payment was beneficial. If he pays it, then the slave belongs to the one paid to, and nothing for the payer, because if the first striker had recourse for anything, the one paid to would have recourse against him again, because his right is in a sound slave, so the recourse of the first striker is not beneficial. And if he ransoms, the master of the later striker is given a choice between payment and ransom, because the slave of the first striker is freed from the injury by ransom and becomes as if he did not injure, even if the later striker inflicted injury upon him. If the first striker dies, his value is in the liability of the second (striker); he pays it or ransoms. If he ransoms him with the value of the deceased, he has recourse in that value for the compensation of the wound of the slave, and it becomes as if he did not injure, rather the first striker injured him. And if the first striker dies, the value stands in his place because he is present. And if he pays him with the compensation of the wound of his slave in his liability, the one paid to is given a choice between payment and ransom because the paid one stands in the place of the deceased who inflicted the wound.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where one slave strikes first (البادئ) and the other retaliates (اللاحق). The ruling: The master of the first striker has a choice (خير) but the text elaborates that the initiation of action from the later striker's master is not effective because the later striker has a right to a sound complete slave. If the later striker's master pays the first striker's slave (who is now wounded) to the first striker's master, the later striker's master can take it back because the slave is not whole. The payment is considered beneficial only if it leads to resolution. If he pays, the slave goes to the recipient and the payer gets nothing because any recourse by the first striker would be met with counter-recourse. If the first striker's master chooses ransom (فداء), then the later striker's master gets to choose between payment and ransom because the first striker's slave becomes free from liability. The passage then discusses the case where the first striker dies: his value is owed by the later striker's master, who may pay or ransom. If he ransoms with the value, he can claim back the compensation for the wound. Essentially, the rights are carefully balanced to ensure each gets their due.

Key Terms
بادئ (badi'): The first striker, the slave who strikes first in the altercation.
لاحق (lahiq): The later striker, the one who retaliates after being struck.
شجة (shajjah): A wound on the head or face; injury.
تخيير (takhyir): The option given to the master to choose between handing over the slave or paying compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The first striker's master keeps the slave and the later striker's master has no further claim.
B) The later striker's master can take the slave back because his right is to a sound slave.
C) The slave is freed.
D) The first striker's master must pay diyah.

Key Takeaway
When one slave strikes first, the master's options are constrained by the later striker's right to a sound slave, preventing unjust enrichment.

Ruling When the Killing Slave Dies
Ruling on master's choice after killing slave dies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state who is given a choice when the killing slave dies and explain the consequence of ransoming or paying.

Core Idea
Upon death of the killing slave, the master of the first striker chooses: ransom or forfeit his own claim.

This passage clarifies a specific scenario in Hanafi diyat law: what happens when the slave who caused a fatal injury dies before compensation is settled? The ruling gives the master of the first striker (the originally injured party) a decisive choice, not the master of the killing slave. Understanding this nuance prevents confusion about who controls the outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and parties
You have a slave (the later striker) who killed another slave (the first striker). The killing slave later dies. Two masters are involved: master of the first striker and master of the killing slave.
2
Identify who is given the choice
The text says 'خير مولى العبد الباديء' — the master of the first striker is given a choice. Note that it is NOT the master of the killing slave.
The common misunderstanding is to reverse the parties.
3
State the options available
The master of the first striker has two options: (1) ransom (فداه) the killing slave by paying compensation, or (2) pay (دفع) by handing over his own slave? Actually the text says 'فإن فداه أو دفع' — if he ransoms him or pays. The precise meaning: if he pays compensation to keep the killing slave, or if he pays by surrendering his own claim? The commentary indicates that 'ransom or pay' means he compensates for the wound or pays the value.
مراجعة
4
Describe the consequence of each option
If he ransoms or pays, then his right (حق) in the wound (شجة) of his slave is voided. In other words, he loses the claim for compensation for the injury to his own slave.
5
Extract the legal rationale (talil)
The basis: the later striker (killer) had previously injured the first striker, so the first striker's master had a right to the wound of his own slave. But when the killing slave dies and the master of the first striker chooses to ransom or pay, he forfeits that right. The rationale is that the death of the killer and the master's action resolve the mutual claims.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن مات العبد القاتل خير مولى العبد الباديء، فإن فداه أو دفع بطل حقه في شجته حين شج اللاحق البادئ كان اللاحق مشجوجاً فثبت حق المولى البادئ في شجة عبده .
And if the killing slave dies, the master of the first striker is given a choice. If he ransoms him or pays, his right in his wound is voided. When the later striker injured the first striker, the later striker was wounded, so the right of the master of the first striker is established in the wound of his slave.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage covers the situation where the slave who killed (the later striker) dies after the altercation. The ruling: The master of the first striker (the one who was originally injured) is given a choice. If the master of the first striker ransoms (pays compensation) or pays (hands over his slave), then his right to compensation for the wound (shajjah) on his slave is voided. The reasoning is that when the later striker injured the first striker, the later striker was also wounded, so the master of the first striker has a right to the wound of his own slave. But if he chooses to ransom or pay, that claim is lost.

Key Terms
قاتل (qatil): The killer, the slave who caused death.
مخير (mukhayyar): Given a choice between options.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the killing slave (the one who inflicted the fatal injury) dies, who is given a choice?
A) The master of the killing slave.
B) The master of the first striker.
C) Both masters equally.
D) The judge.

Key Takeaway
Upon the death of the killing slave, the master of the first striker has the decisive choice: ransoming or paying voids his right to compensation for his own slave's wound.

Ruling When the First Striker Dies from an Unrelated Cause
Explains ruling when the first striker dies from something other than the injury, and the later striker survives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options available to the master of the later striker and explain the legal consequences of each, including the effect of refusal to pay compensation.

Core Idea
When the first striker dies from another cause, the master of the later striker has a choice between forgiveness or payment with recourse.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a nuanced scenario in diyat: two slaves fight; the first striker dies from an unrelated cause, while the later striker survives. The ruling outlines the options for the master of the later striker and clarifies the legal effects of each choice, including the consequences of refusal to pay compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and parties
Understand that there are two slaves: one who struck first (al-badi') and died from another cause, and the later striker (al-lahiq) who survives. The masters are the owners of these slaves.
Free persons are not involved; this is about slave injuries.
2
State the first option: forgiveness
The master of the later striker can choose to forgive (afw) the master of the first striker, resulting in no claims between them.
Forgiveness here means relinquishing the right to claim compensation for the injury to his slave.
3
State the second option: pay compensation then claim
The master can pay the compensation for the wound of the later striker to the master of the first striker, then demand either the slave or ransom from the other master.
This involves a reciprocal exchange.
4
Explain the effect of refusal to pay
If the master of the first striker refuses to pay compensation, his right is voided as if he had chosen forgiveness.
This is because he was given a choice and his refusal implies forgiveness.
5
Summarize the legal purification
The goal is to ensure each master receives his due; payment purifies the first striker from liability, making it as if the later striker injured him.
This clarifies the reasoning behind the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو مات البادئ من شيء آخر سوى الجناية وبقي اللاحق خير المولى ويقال له إذا شئت ادفع واعف عن مولى اللاحق ولا سبيل لواحد منهما على الآخر، وإن شئت ادفع أرش شجة اللاحق وطالبه، فإن دفع إلى صاحبه أرش عبده يرجع بأرش جناية عبده فيدفع مولى اللاحق عبده أو يفده ؛ أما العفو فلأنه مولى البادئ بجنايته وإذا دفع كان لمولى اللاحق أن يطالبه بأرش شجة عبده وكان لمولى البادئ أن يدفع إليه العبد المدفوع ثانياً ليبرأ عن حقه فلا يفيد الدفع. وإنما دفع أرش شجة اللاحق لأنه متى دفع أرش عبد اللاحق فقد طهر البادئ عن الجناية وصار كأنه لم يجن، وإنما جنى عليه العبد اللاحق فيخاطب مولى اللاحق بالدفع أو الفداء وأي ذلك اختار لا يبقى لواحد منهما على صاحبه سبيل لأنه وصل إلى كل واحد منهما حقه، وإن أبى مولى البادئ أن يدفع الأرش فلا تعلق له في عنق الحر لأن مولى البادئ كان مخيراً بين العفو وبين دفع الأرش والمطالبة بشجة عبده، فإذا امتنع من دفع الأرش صار مختاراً للعفو وصار كأنه قال عفوتك عن حق فبطل حقه.
And if the first striker dies from something other than the injury, and the later striker remains, the master (of the later striker?) is given a choice. It is said to him: If you wish, pay (the slave) and forgive the master of the later striker, and there is no claim for either against the other. If you wish, pay the compensation of the wound of the later striker and claim (it). If he pays to his companion the compensation of his slave, he has recourse for the compensation of the injury of his slave; then the master of the later striker pays his slave or ransoms him. As for forgiveness, it is because he is the master of the first striker by his injury. And if he pays, then the master of the later striker can claim from him the compensation of the wound of his slave, and the master of the first striker can pay the paid slave a second time to free himself from his right, so payment is not beneficial. Rather, he pays the compensation of the wound of the later striker because whenever he pays the compensation of the slave of the later striker, he has purified the first striker from the injury and it becomes as if he did not injure, and rather the later striker injured him. Then the master of the later striker is addressed with payment or ransom. Whichever he chooses, there remains no claim for either against the other because each has received his right. And if the master of the first striker refuses to pay the compensation, then he has no claim in the liability of the free person because the master of the first striker was given a choice between forgiveness and payment of compensation and claiming for the wound of his slave. So when he refrains from paying the compensation, he becomes as if he chose forgiveness, and it is as if he said: 'I forgive you for the right,' so his right is voided.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where the first striker (البادئ) dies from a cause unrelated to the fight, while the later striker (اللاحق) survives. The ruling: The master (presumably of the later striker) is given a choice. He has two options: (1) Pay the slave (hand over his slave to the other) and forgive the other master, resulting in no further claims. (2) Pay the compensation for the wound of the later striker and then claim it back? Actually the text is complex. The master may pay the compensation of the wound of the later striker to the other master, and then the other master has to pay his slave or ransom. If the master of the first striker refuses to pay the compensation, then he loses his right to claim anything, as if he chose forgiveness. The reasoning is about purification of liability and ensuring that each receives their due.

Key Terms
عفو (afw): Forgiveness, relinquishing the right to compensation.
حر (hurr): Free person (as opposed to slave). Here 'عنق الحر' might mean 'the liability of the free person' i.e., the master.

A) He still retains his right to claim.
B) His right is voided as if he had forgiven.
C) He must be forced by the judge.
D) He forfeits his slave.

Key Takeaway
The master of the later striker has a choice; the master of the first striker's refusal to pay forfeits his right.

Ruling When the Later Striker Dies and the First Survives
Explains ruling when the later striker dies and the first striker survives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two options for the master of the first striker when the later striker dies, and explain the legal consequence of each option regarding liability and recourse.

Core Idea
Paying the substitute voids the first striker's right; ransoming purifies him and prevents further claim.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a specific scenario in diyat (blood money) where two slaves have wounded each other, one later (اللاحق) dies, and the first (البادئ) survives. The master of the first striker faces a decisive choice that determines whether his slave remains liable. Understanding this choice clarifies how Hanafi law prevents circular claims and ensures finality in compensation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and parties
The later striker (اللاحق) dies; the first striker (البادئ) survives. The master of the first striker is given a choice.
2
Option 1: Payment (دفع)
If the master pays (hands over the later striker's slave as substitute), his right to compensation is voided. However, the first striker is not purified from his own liability.
3
Option 2: Ransom (فداء)
If the master ransoms (pays the compensation أرش), he keeps his slave. The first striker is purified from the injury, so the later striker's master cannot reclaim the compensation again.
4
Distinguish the underlying reason
In ransom, purification occurs (طهر). In payment, no purification (لم يظهر), so liability attaches to the substitute slave.
5
Note the result regarding recourse
If the first striker's master later tries to claim compensation for his own wound, the later striker's master would have recourse against him, making such a claim pointless.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو مات اللاحق وبقي البادئ خير مولاه. فإن دفعه بطل حقه، وإن فداه بأرش فداه عبده وفي الفداء لأن البادئ طهر عن الجناية فلا يكون لمولى اللاحق أن يسترجع منه الأرش ثانياً فأما الدفع لم يظهر عن الجناية فبقي حق مولى اللاحق متعلقاً بما فات بالشجة من العبد البادئ والعبد المدفوع بدله فيتعلق حقه ببدله، فلو رجع مولى البادئ بأرش شجته كان لمولى اللاحق أن منه يسترجع كان متعلقاً بالفائت من الفائت البادئ فلا يفيد الرجوع
And if the later striker dies and the first striker remains, his master is given a choice. If he pays him (the later striker's slave?), his right is voided. And if he ransoms him with the compensation, he ransoms his slave. And in ransom, because the first striker is purified from the injury, so the master of the later striker cannot reclaim from him the compensation a second time. As for payment, he is not purified from the injury, so the right of the master of the later striker remains attached to what was lost by the wound from the first striker's slave, and the paid slave is its substitute, so his right attaches to its substitute. If the master of the first striker had recourse for the compensation of his wound, the master of the later striker could have recourse from him, and it would be attached to the lost from the first striker, so recourse is not beneficial.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This section deals with the case where the later striker (اللاحق) dies, but the first striker (البادئ) survives. The master of the first striker is given a choice. If he pays (hands over the later striker's slave? Actually 'دفعه' - pays him), his right is voided. If he ransoms (pays compensation), he ransoms his slave (i.e., keeps him). In the case of ransom, the first striker is purified from liability, so the master of the later striker cannot reclaim the compensation again. But in the case of payment, the first striker is not purified, so the master of the later striker's right remains attached to the loss from the first striker's slave, and since the paid slave is a substitute, his right attaches to that substitute. If the master of the first striker then tries to claim compensation for his wound, the master of the later striker would have recourse against him, so it's not beneficial. The ruling aims to prevent circular recourse.

Key Terms
بدل (badal): Substitute, replacement; here, the slave given as compensation.
تعذر الرجوع (ta'addhur al-ruju'): Impossibility of recourse or claiming back.
دفع (daf'): Payment; here, handing over the later striker's slave as a substitute.
فداء (fida'): Ransom; paying compensation to keep the slave.
أرش (arsh): Compensation for wounds, fixed damages.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) He can still claim compensation later.
C) The later striker's master can claim again.
D) The slave is freed.

Key Takeaway
The choice given to the first striker's master determines whether liability is purified or transferred to a substitute, preventing circular claims.

Liabilities When a Wounded Slave Is Killed by the Original Aggressor
Expands ruling on mutual injuries among slaves turning into homicide.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the compensation owed by the master of the first striker who kills the wounded later striker, and apply the choice between paying the slave or ransoming.

Core Idea
Killing a wounded victim: owe both wound compensation and full value, with equitable distribution between masters.

After a fight between two slaves, both survive but one is wounded. Later, the original aggressor kills the wounded one. This lesson examines the complex web of liabilities: what the killer's master must pay, the choice he has, and how the payments are split to satisfy the rights of both masters. The ruling ensures that no party is unjustly enriched or deprived.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence of events
Trace the events: two slaves fight; both survive; the first striker (البادئ) later kills the later striker (اللاحق) while the later striker is still wounded from the earlier fight. Note who is alive at each stage.
The later striker is 'jariḥan' (wounded) at the time of killing.
2
Determine the obligations of the first striker's master
The master of the first striker owes: (a) the wound compensation (أرش الشجة) for the earlier wound, and (b) the full value of the killed slave (قيمة المقتول) since he killed him. The later striker's wound does not reduce his value for the homicide liability.
The value is assessed at the time of killing, while he is wounded.
3
Analyze the choice (تخيير) given to the master
The master has two options: (1) دفع (hand over his own slave to the master of the killed) — then he owes nothing more; or (2) فداء (ransom) — i.e., pay the compensation in money. The text explains the consequences of each.
The choice is the master's, not the slave's.
4
Trace the distribution when ransom is chosen
When ransom is chosen, the master pays the wound compensation of the killed and the value of the killed. Then from that value, the master of the first striker takes the wound compensation for his own slave (since the later striker had wounded the first striker). The remainder goes to the master of the killed.
The wound compensation for the living (first striker's slave) is deducted from the value of the killed.
5
Understand the legal reasoning (تعليل)
The distribution ensures that the right of the master of the first striker (for the wound on his slave) is satisfied from the value of the later striker while he was wounded. After that, the remaining value belongs to the master of the killed, as it is the substitute for his slave.
The later striker's liability for wounding the first striker is taken into account.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو برئا ثم قتل البادئ اللاحق جريحاً كان في عنق البادئ أرض اللاحق وقيمته ويخير بين دفعه وفدائه، فإن دفعه فلا شيء له لما بينا، وأن فداه فداه بأرش الشجة وقيمة المقتول لأن البادئ شج اللاحق ثم قتله مشجوجاً فيلزمه أرش الشجة وقيمته مشجوجاً متى اختار الفداء ويسلم أرش الشجة المقتول لمولاه خاصة ويكون أرش شجة الحي في هذه القيمة يأخذ مولاه منها وما بقي لمولى المقتول لأن حق مولى البادئ إنما يثبت في حق اللاحق وهو مشجوج لأنه حين جنى على البادئ وهو مشجوج فيأخذ من قيمته مشجوجاً أرش شجة البادئ، فإن فضل منه شيء يكون لمولى اللاحق لأنه بدل عبده وقد فرغ عن حق الغير.
And if they both survive, then the first striker kills the later striker while wounded, the first striker owes the compensation (arsh) of the later striker and his value, and he is given a choice between paying him (the slave) or ransoming him. If he pays him, then he has nothing, as we have stated. If he ransoms him, he ransoms him with the compensation of the wound and the value of the killed, because the first striker wounded the later striker and then killed him while wounded, so he is liable for the wound compensation and his value while wounded whenever he chooses ransom. And he delivers the wound compensation of the killed to his master specifically. And the wound compensation of the living (i.e., the first striker's slave) is taken from this value: his master takes from it and what remains belongs to the master of the killed, because the right of the master of the first striker is only established in the right of the later striker while he is wounded. When he injured the first striker while he was wounded, he takes from his value while wounded the wound compensation of the first striker. If anything remains, it belongs to the master of the later striker, because it is the substitute for his slave and he has discharged the right of another.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage covers the scenario where both slaves survive the initial fight, but later the first striker kills the later striker while he is still wounded from the earlier fight. The ruling: The first striker owes two things: the compensation (arsh) for the wound he inflicted earlier and the full value of the later striker (since he killed him). The master of the first striker has a choice: either pay the slave (hand over his slave to the master of the killed) or ransom (pay compensation). If he pays the slave, he gets nothing back. If he ransoms, he must pay both the wound compensation and the value of the killed (based on his value while wounded). The distribution: the wound compensation of the killed goes to his master; then from the value, the master of the first striker takes the compensation for the wound on his own slave (since the later striker had wounded the first striker), and the remainder goes to the master of the killed. The reasoning ensures that the rights of both masters are satisfied.

Key Terms
قيمة (qimah): Value, market price of the slave.
أرش الشجة (arsh al-shajjah): Compensation for a head wound.
دفع (daf'): Handing over the slave (the first striker) to the master of the killed to settle the liability.
فداء (fida'): Ransom; paying monetary compensation instead of handing over the slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is paid separately by the master of the later striker.
B) It is deducted from the value of the killed slave.
C) It is not recovered because the first striker killed the later striker.
D) It is waived due to the homicide.

Key Takeaway
The master of the first striker who kills a wounded victim must account for both the original wound compensation and the homicide value, with the wound compensation for his own slave deducted from the homicide value to ensure fairness.

Ruling When One Slave Kills Another After Recovery and the First Striker is Unknown
Explains ruling when one kills the other after both recover, but it is unknown who struck first initially

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling and the qiyas-based reasoning when a slave kills another after recovery and the first striker is unknown.

Core Idea
Ignorance of the first striker gives the killer's master a choice: pay his slave or ransom him.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a nuanced diyat case: two slaves fight, both recover, then one kills the other, but it is unknown who struck the first blow. The Hanafi ruling provides a clear framework based on analogy with the case where the first striker is dead, ensuring justice despite uncertainty. The master of the killer is given a choice between handing over his slave (with partial compensation) or ransoming him with the full value of the killed slave.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Two slaves fought, both recovered, then one killed the other. It is unknown who struck first initially.
The uncertainty is about the first striker in the initial fight, not the final killing.
2
State the ruling
The master of the killer is given a choice (خير). He may either hand over his slave (payment) or ransom his slave by paying the full value of the killed slave as sound.
The choice exists because the first striker cannot be identified.
3
Understand the payment option
If the master pays his slave, he receives half the compensation (arsh) of the wound on the killed slave, and the value of his own slave while wounded (since he was also injured in the initial fight).
This is because the payment slave stands in place of the killed slave.
4
Understand the ransom option
If the master ransoms his slave, he pays the full value of the killed slave as sound. This is because the killer (the master's slave) is considered the first striker in the final killing.
The ransom is the full value, not adjusted for the initial wound.
5
Trace the qiyas reasoning
The difficulty (ta‘adhdhur) of initiating with the first striker due to ignorance is analogized to the impossibility of initiation when the first striker is dead. In both cases, the ruling is the same: the master of the killer is given a choice.
This is a qiyas with a clear illah: inability to identify or reach the first striker.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قتل أحدهما صاحبه بعد ما برئا ولا يعلم البادئ بالشجة خير مولى القاتل لأنه تعذرت البداءة بالبادئ للجهالة، ولو تعذرت البداءة بسبب موت البادي تعذر القتل فكذا هذا فإن دفع عبده كان له نصف أرش شجة المقتول وعلى قيمته مشجوجاً فيأخذ الذي دفعه من حصته فيمته مشجوجاً من العبد المدفوع أو يفديه لأن القاتل بالدفع قام مقام المقتول لحماً ودماً فصار كأن المقتول بقي حياً لمولاه يرجع بنصف أرش شجة عبده متى اختار الدفع فكذا إذا دفع بدله وأن اختار مولى القاتل فداه بقيمة المقتول صحيحاً لأن القاتل هو البادئ بالشجة. شج عبداً صحيحاً ثم قتله فعليه قيمة عبد صحيح، وإن كان القاتل هو اللاحق فقد شج البادي وهو صحيح ثم قتله كان المولى القاتل أن يفدي عبده بقيمة المقتول صحيحاً ويرجع بأرش الشجة في الفداء بعد ما يدفع إلى مولى العبد المقتول نصف أرش شجته لأن القيمة قامت مقام المقتول ولو كان المقتول حياً وقد شج كل واحد منهما صاحبه ولا يعلم البادئ منهما يرجع كل واحد منهما فيما دفع إلى صاحبه بنصف أرش شجة عبده، والمدفوع إليه يتخير بين الفداء وبين ما يخص نصف أرش الشجة من العبد المدفوع إليه فكذا تركته .
And if one of them kills his companion after they both recover, and it is not known who was the first striker in the wound, the master of the killer is given a choice because the initiation with the first striker is impossible due to ignorance. And if initiation is impossible due to the death of the first striker, it is impossible to kill, so similar to this. So if he pays his slave, he gets half the compensation of the wound of the killed, and the value of his slave while wounded: he takes what he paid from his share, and the value while wounded from the paid slave, or ransoms him? Because the killer by payment stands in the place of the killed in flesh and blood, so it is as if the killed remained alive for his master, he recovers half the compensation of his slave's wound whenever he chooses payment, so similarly if he pays his substitute. And if the master of the killer chooses ransom, he ransoms him with the value of the killed as sound, because the killer is the first striker in the wound. He wounded a sound slave and then killed him, so he owes the value of a sound slave. If the killer is the later striker, he wounded the first striker while sound and then killed him; then the killer's master may ransom his slave with the value of the killed as sound, and he recovers the wound compensation in the ransom after he pays to the master of the killed half the compensation of his wound, because the value stands in place of the killed. If the killed were alive and each had wounded the other and it is not known who was the first striker, each would recover from what he paid to the other half the compensation of his slave's wound, and the one paid to would have the choice between ransom and what pertains to half the compensation of the wound from the paid slave, so similarly his estate.

Commentary
This passage addresses the complex scenario where both slaves recover from their initial fight, then one kills the other, but it is unknown who was the original first striker (i.e., who struck the first blow in the initial fight). The ruling: The master of the killer is given a choice because the identity of the first striker is unknown. The reasoning draws an analogy with the case where the first striker dies (which makes initiation impossible). The text is complex. Or (2) ransom his slave by paying the full value of the killed as a sound slave. The text then discusses the subcase where the killer was actually the later striker, and then the rules differ. It also mentions the scenario where both had wounded each other and the first striker is unknown, each takes half compensation. The passage is dense but aims to provide a detailed legal analysis.

Key Terms
جهالة (jahalah): Ignorance, uncertainty about the facts, specifically the identity of the first striker.
بداءة (bida'ah): Initiation, the act of beginning the aggression.
دفع (daf'): Payment by handing over the killer slave to the victim's master.
فداء (fida'): Ransom, paying the full value of the killed slave to keep the killer slave.

When the first striker is unknown in a diyat case, the master of the killer is given a choice between payment and ransom, analogized to the case of the first striker's death.

Mutual Kill Between Two Slaves: Avenger's Options
Ruling on mutual killing between slaves with avenger's options

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mutual killing between two slaves and explain the avenger's choices and their consequences.

Core Idea
If the avenger forgives, all claims vanish; if he claims, compensation flows with a choice for the living master.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with a specific scenario in the chapter of diyat where two slaves injure each other and one is killed. The ruling turns on whether the avenger of the killed (the slave's master) demands compensation or forgives. Understanding this ruling clarifies how Hanafi law resolves reciprocal claims in injury cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Recognize the two slaves: the first striker (who strikes first and survives) and the later striker (who strikes second and is killed). Their masters are the legal actors.
The master of the killed slave is called 'wali al-maqtul'.
2
Scenario A: Avenger does not claim
If the avenger of the killed does not demand compensation (i.e., forgives), then no claims remain between any parties. Neither master owes anything.
Forgiveness is a valid option that settles all.
3
Scenario B: Avenger claims
If the avenger does claim, the process begins: first, compensation (arsh) for the wound on the first striker is paid to his master. Then the master of the living slave is given a choice: either hand over his slave or pay the full value of the killed slave.
The choice belongs to the master of the living, not the avenger.
4
Understand the reasoning
The later striker was already wounded (due to the first strike) before killing the first striker. Therefore, his master (the avenger) has a legitimate claim for that wound; but the first striker's death must also be compensated. The law provides a structured settlement.
The talil (reasoning) ensures each party receives their due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قتل البادئ اللاحق فإن لم يطلب ولي المقتول الجناية لم يكن لأحدهما على صاحبه شيء لأن مولى المقتول يخير بين العفو والفداء بأرش الشجة الثانية، وإن طلب الجناية بدأ عنه بأرش الحي ثم خير مولى الحي بين أن يدفع عبده أو يفديه بقيمة المقتول ويسلم ذلك لولي المقتول لأن العبد اللاحق قبل البادئ مشجوجاً فيخير مولاه بين دفعه وفدائه بقيمته مشجوجاً وأي ذلك فعل لا يبقى لأحدهما على صاحبه سبيل لأنه وصل إلى كل واحد منهما حقه.
And if the first striker kills the later striker, and the avenger of the killed does not claim the injury, then none of them has any claim against the other, because the master of the killed is given a choice between forgiveness and ransom with the compensation of the second wound. If he claims the injury, he begins with the compensation of the living (i.e., the first striker's wound), then the master of the living is given a choice between paying his slave or ransoming him with the value of the killed, and he delivers that to the avenger of the killed, because the later striker was wounded before the first striker, so his master is given a choice between paying him (the slave) or ransoming him with his value while wounded. Commentary
This passage discusses the case where the first striker kills the later striker. If the avenger (ولي المقتول) does not claim the injury (meaning he does not demand retribution or compensation for the killing), then neither party has any claim against the other. The master of the killed has a choice: forgive or demand ransom for the second wound (the wound from the killing). If he does claim the injury (i.e., demands compensation), then he first receives the compensation for the wound on the first striker (since the later striker had wounded him earlier), and then the master of the living (the first striker's master) is given a choice: either hand over his slave or ransom him with the value of the killed slave, which goes to the avenger. The reasoning is that the later striker was already wounded before the first striker struck, so his master has a choice. After the settlement, no further claims remain.

Key Terms
ولي المقتول (wali al-maqtul): The legal guardian or heir of the killed person, entitled to claim diyah or qisas.
أرش (arsh): Compensation for a wound, usually a fixed amount depending on the severity.
فداء (fidā'): Ransom; paying a sum to free a slave or avoid handing him over.

Diyah Distribution After Partial Forgiveness in Mixed-Culpability Killing
Ruling on diyah distribution after partial forgiveness in mixed-culpability killing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on diyah distribution when one of two heirs of an intentional killer forgives and identify the shares given to the accidental heir and the remaining intentional heir.

Core Idea
When one heir of intentional killing forgives, the accidental heir gets full diyah, the other intentional heir gets half.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq concerning a case where two slaves cause a death—one intentionally and one accidentally. When one of the two heirs of the intentional killer exercises his right to forgive, the distribution of diyah is adjusted. The passage, though textually corrupt due to OCR issues, conveys a distinct Hanafi rule about how diyah is apportioned between the heirs of the accidental and intentional killers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actors and their roles
Determine who the killers are (slaves), their acts (one 'amd, one khata), and the heirs (two for 'amd, one for khata).
The victim is a relative (qarib) of the slave owners, who are also the heirs.
2
Analyze the forgiveness action
One of the two heirs of the intentional killer forgives. In Hanafi law, forgiveness in intentional killing extinguishes the right to qisas and may reduce or redirect diyah claims.
The forgiving heir forfeits his own share of diyah.
3
Derive the distribution after forgiveness
The remaining diyah is paid: full diyah to the accidental killer's heir, and half of a diyah to the remaining heir of the intentional killer.
The text says 'فدى بالدية لولي الخطأ وبنصفها لأحد وليي العمد' - the total appears to be 1.5 diyah, which suggests separate obligations for each killing.
4
Identify the underlying principle
The ruling reflects that accidental killing always incurs a full diyah obligation, while intentional killing's diyah is subject to the heirs' choices (qisas or diyah, and forgiveness).
This ensures that the accidental killer's heir is fully compensated regardless of forgiveness on the intentional side.

Liability After Pardon and Substitution in Slave Homicide
Commentary on the effect of pardon on liability in mutual slave homicide

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when one heir of intentional killing pardons and explain how the owner's right transfers to the substitute slave.

Core Idea
A pardon voids qisas but the owner's right attaches to the substitute (badal).

This lesson examines the opening part of the passage, where two slaves kill a relative, one intentionally and one accidentally. When one of the two heirs of the intentional killing pardons, the right to qisas is partially waived, and the owner's claim shifts from the offending slave to the slave handed over as a substitute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial scenario and pardoning effect
Read the first sentence: two slaves killed a relative, one intentional, one accidental. One of the two heirs of the intentional killing pardons. The pardon voids the right to qisas for that share.
The other heir retains the right to his share.
2
Determine the outcome of pardon on financial claims
The pardon does not eliminate financial liability. The owner of the later aggressor cannot reclaim the compensation (arsh) from the owner of the initial aggressor a second time.
This is because his right is now attached to the substitute slave.
3
Understand the attachment to substitute
The passage explains that the right of the owner of the later aggressor remains attached to what was lost (the wound) from the initial aggressor and to the substitute slave handed over.
The substitute stands in the place of the offending slave.
4
Apply the principle of non-reclamation
If the owner of the initial aggressor tries to reclaim the arsh from the other owner, the later owner can reclaim it back, because the right was already attached to the lost value.
This prevents double recovery.

يكن لأحدهما على صاحبه شيء لأن مولى المقتول يخير بين العفو والفداء بأرش الشجة الثانية، وإن طلب الجناية بدأ عنه بأرش الحي ثم خير مولى الحي بين أن يدفع عبده أو يفديه بقيمة المقتول ويسلم ذلك لولي المقتول البادئ بالشجة خير مولى القاتل لأنه تعذرت البداءة بالبادئ للجهالة، ولو تعذرت البداءة بسبب موت البادي تعذر القتل فكذا هذا فإن دفع عبده كان له نصف أرش شجة المقتول وعلى قيمته مشجوجاً فيأخذ الذي دفعه من With the blood-money for the heir of the accidental killing and half of it for one of the two heirs of the intentional killing, their two slaves killed their relative, so one of them pardoned, so it becomes void because his right is the offense, so the owner of the later aggressor cannot reclaim the compensation from him a second time. As for the handover, he did not appear from the offense, so the right of the owner of the later aggressor remains attached to what was lost by the head wound from the initial aggressor and the slave handed over as a substitute, so his right attaches to his substitute. So if the owner of the initial aggressor reclaims the compensation for his head wound, the owner of the later aggressor can reclaim it from him, it was attached to the lost from the lost of the initial aggressor, so the reclaim is not beneficial. If he ransoms him, he ransoms him with the compensation for the head wound and the value of the killed person, because the initial aggressor wounded the later aggressor then killed him while wounded, so he owes the compensation for the head wound and his value while wounded whenever he chooses ransom. Whatever he does, neither has any recourse against the other because each has reached his right. If one kills the other after both recover and the initial aggressor of the head wound is unknown, the owner of the killer is given the choice because beginning with the initial aggressor is not possible due to ignorance. If beginning is not possible due to the death of the initial aggressor, then execution is not possible; likewise here. If he hands over his slave, he is entitled to half the compensation for the head wound of the killed and his value while wounded, so the one who handed over takes from his share his value while wounded from the handed-over slave, or he ransoms him, because the killer, by handing over, stands in the place of the killed in flesh and blood, so it is as if the killed remained alive for his owner, who reclaims half the compensation for the head wound of his slave whenever he chooses handover; likewise if he hands over his substitute. If the owner of the killer chooses to ransom, he ransoms him with the value of the killed as healthy, because the killer is the initial aggressor of the head wound. One wounds a healthy slave then kills him, so he owes the value of a healthy slave. If the killer is the later aggressor, and he wounded the initial aggressor while he was healthy then killed him, the owner of the killer can ransom his slave with the value of the killed as healthy and reclaim the compensation for the head wound from the ransom after he pays the owner of the killed slave half the compensation for his head wound, because the value stands in place of the killed. If the killed were alive and each had wounded the other and the initial aggressor of them is unknown, each reclaims from what he paid to the other half the compensation for the head wound of his slave, and the one to whom it is handed over is given the choice between ransom and what corresponds to half the compensation for the head wound from the slave handed over to him; likewise his estate.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expanding on the rulings of mutual injuries and homicide between two slaves. It begins by considering a scenario where one slave kills intentionally and the other accidentally, and one of the heirs of the intentional killing pardons. When one heir pardons, the right to retaliation (qisas) is waived for that share, and the remaining share becomes a financial claim. The passage then explores various permutations: if the initial aggressor wounds the later aggressor and then kills him while still wounded, the initial aggressor's owner must pay compensation for the wound and the value of the killed slave. The owner of the initial aggressor has the option to hand over the slave or pay ransom. The rules shift if the slaves recover and then one kills the other, or if the identity of the initial aggressor is unknown. The key principle is that the owner's rights attach to substitutes (badal) and that the sequence of events determines liability. The commentator uses legal reasoning (ta'lil) to justify each ruling, emphasizing that the slave's value is assessed based on his condition at the time of the offense.

Key Terms
جناية (jinayah): An offense or crime, specifically physical harm or homicide.
أرش (arsh): Monetary compensation for bodily injury, less than full blood-money.
شجة (shajjah): A head wound specifically, often used generically for wounds in this context.
فداء (fida'): Ransom payment to free a slave from liability or to substitute for his handover.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The right is doubled because of the pardon.

Key Takeaway
A pardon by one heir in intentional killing does not extinguish the owner's right to financial compensation; it shifts to the substitute slave.

Division of the Slave in Diyat: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Proportional Reduction
Matn and commentary on dividing the slave's value

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn in dividing the slave when one intentional heir pardons, and apply the rule of 'awl (proportional reduction) to competing claims.

Core Idea
When claims compete, rights are reduced proportionally; the Sahibayn apply a staged approach, while Abu Hanifa applies a direct ratio.

This lesson examines a specific case from the law of diyat: two slaves, one kills intentionally, the other accidentally. One of the two heirs of the intentional killing pardons. How is the intentional killer's slave divided among the claimants? The Hanafi school has two views: Abu Hanifa's direct proportional division and the Sahibayn's staged division. Understanding this dispute clarifies the principle of 'awl (proportional reduction) in competing claims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimants and their rights
Two killings: one intentional (amad) and one accidental (khata'). The accidental killing yields a diyah of 10,000 dirhams due to the accidental heir. The intentional killing yields qisas (retaliation) or diyah. Two intentional heirs; if one pardons, the other's right becomes 5,000 dirhams. So the claimants are the accidental heir (10,000 right) and the non-pardoning intentional heir (5,000 right).
Rights are attached to the slave's value.
2
Understand the effect of the pardon
The pardoning intentional heir forfeits his share of qisas, so his portion does not compete for the slave. Only the non-pardoning intentional heir and the accidental heir have claims on the slave.
The slave is the intentional killer; he can be ransomed or handed over.
3
Contrast Abu Hanifa's direct ratio method
Abu Hanifa divides the slave according to the ratio of their rights: 10,000 : 5,000 = 2:1. Thus the accidental heir gets 2/3, the non-pardoning intentional heir gets 1/3.
This is pure 'awl (proportional reduction) on the whole slave.
4
Contrast the Sahibayn's staged method
The Sahibayn argue that half the slave is already the accidental heir's without dispute (since the accidental killing's 10,000 is fixed and half of the slave's value is 5,000? Actually, they consider the slave's value as 15,000, so half is 7,500? Wait, careful: In the Sahibayn's view, they say half the slave (i.e., half the value) is for the accidental heir without dispute. The other half is disputed equally between the accidental heir (who also claims part of that half) and the non-pardoning intentional heir. That half is divided equally, giving the accidental heir an additional quarter, total 3/4, and the intentional heir gets 1/4.
This method separates an undisputed portion before applying 'awl.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Abu Hanifa gives the accidental heir 2/3 (66.67%), the Sahibayn give 3/4 (75%). The difference is 1/12 of the slave's value. The commentary defends Abu Hanifa, noting that the accidental heir has a right over the entire slave, so no portion is undisputed.
Mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال رحمه الله : (وإن قتل أحدهما عمداً والآخر خطأ فعفا أحد وليي العمد فدى بالدية لولي الخطأ وبنصفها لأحد وليي العمد لأن حقهما في الدية عشر آلاف وحق وليي العبد في القصاص، فإن عفا أحدهما انقلب نصيب الآخر مالاً وهو نصف الدية خمسة آلاف، فإذا فداه بخمسة عشر ألف درهم عشرة آلاف لولي الخطأ وخمسة آلاف لغير العافي من وليي العمد، وإن دفعه إليهم أثلاثاً ثلثاه لولي الخطأ وثلثه للساكت من ولي العمد بطريق العمد لأن حقهم في الدية كذلك فيضرب ولياً الخطأ بعشرة آلاف ويضرب غير العافي من وليي العمد بخمسة ألاف، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله. وقال أبو يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله : يدفعه أرباعاً بطريق المنازعة ثلاثة أرباعه لوليي الخطأ وربعه لغير العافي من وليي العمد لأن نصفه سلم الولي الخطأ بلا منازعة فاستوت منازعتهم في النصف الآخر فينتصف . فإن قيل : ينبغي أن يسلم للمولى ربع العبد في هذه المسألة وهي نصيب العافي من وليي العمد ويدفع ثلاثة أرباعه إليهم تقسم بينهم على قدر حقوقهم كما سلم له النصف وهو نصيب العافين قلنا : لا يمكن ذلك هنا لأن لوليي الخطأ استحقاق كله ولم يسقط من حقهما شيء، وهذا لأن حق كل واحد من الفريقين تعلق بكل الرقبة في المسألتين غير أنه لما عفا ولي كل قتيل سقط حق العافين على الرقبة في المسألة الأولى وخلى نصيبهما منه عن حقهما وصار كذلك للمولى وهو النصف بخلاف ما نحن فيه فإن حق ولي الخطأ ثابت في الكل على حاله وكانت الرقبة كلها مستحقة لهما والنصف لغير العافي من ولي العمد فلهذا افترقا فيقسمونها كلها على قدر حقوقهم بطريق العول والمنازعة ولهذه المسألة نظائر ذكرناها في كتاب الدعوى من الكتاب بأصولها الذي نشأ منها الخلاف بتوفيق الله تعالى فلا نعيدها.
He (the author), may Allah have mercy on him, said: (And if one of them kills intentionally and the other accidentally, and one of the two heirs of the intentional killing pardons, then he ransoms with the blood-money for the heir of the accidental killing and half of it for one of the two heirs of the intentional killing, because their right in the blood-money is ten thousand dirhams, and the right of the two heirs of the intentional killing is in retaliation. So if one of them pardons, the share of the other becomes property, which is half the blood-money, five thousand. So if he ransoms him for fifteen thousand dirhams, ten thousand go to the heir of the accidental killing and five thousand to the non-pardoning one of the two heirs of the intentional killing. If he hands him over to them by thirds, two-thirds to the heir of the accidental killing and one-third to the silent one of the two heirs of the intentional killing by way of the intentional [correction: by way of 'awl (proportional reduction)] because their right in the blood-money is like that. So the two heirs of the accidental killing have ten thousand shares and the non-pardoning one of the two heirs of the intentional killing has five thousand shares. This is according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, said: He hands him over by fourths by way of dispute: three-quarters to the two heirs of the accidental killing and one-quarter to the non-pardoning one of the two heirs of the intentional killing, because half of him was surrendered to the heir of the accidental killing without dispute, so their dispute became equal in the other half, so it is divided in half. If it is said: It should be that one-quarter of the slave is surrendered to the owner in this case, which is the share of the pardoning one of the two heirs of the intentional killing, and he hands over three-quarters to them divided among them according to the measure of their rights, just as half was surrendered to him which is the share of the pardoners. We say: That is not possible here because the two heirs of the accidental killing have entitlement to the whole, and nothing of their right has fallen away. This is because the right of each of the two groups attached to the entire slave in the two cases, except that when the heir of each killed person pardoned, the right of the pardoners on the slave fell in the first case and they vacated their share from it regarding their right, and it became for the owner, which is half. Unlike our case here, because the right of the heir of the accidental killing is established in the whole as it was, and the entire slave was owed to them, and half to the non-pardoning one of the two heirs of the intentional killing. For this reason they differed: they divide all of it according to the measure of their rights by way of 'awl and dispute. This case has parallels which we mentioned in the book of claims from this book with its principles from which the disagreement arose, by the grace of Allah. We do not repeat them.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This lesson contains the matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq and its commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. The case: two slaves, one kills intentionally (the intentional killer) and the other kills accidentally (the accidental killer). The intentional killer has two heirs (or guardians) who have the right to either demand qisas (retaliation) or accept diyah (blood-money). The accidental killing only entails diyah (10,000 dirhams). If one of the two intentional heirs pardons, his share of qisas is waived, and the other intentional heir's right becomes purely financial (5,000 dirhams). The slave who is the intentional killer is then ransomed for a total of 15,000 dirhams: 10,000 to the accidental heir and 5,000 to the non-pardoning intentional heir, according to Abu Hanifa. If the slave is handed over instead of ransomed, the division is by thirds: 2/3 to the accidental heir and 1/3 to the non-pardoning intentional heir. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) disagree: they say the division should be by fourths: 3/4 to the accidental heir and 1/4 to the non-pardoning intentional heir. Their reasoning: the accidental heir already has half the slave's value without dispute (due to the accidental killing), so the remaining half is disputed between the non-pardoning intentional heir and the accidental heir (who also claims a share of that half as part of his full entitlement). They divide that half equally. The commentary then defends Abu Hanifa's view by noting that the accidental heir's right encompasses the entire slave (due to the full 10,000 diyah for accidental killing), unlike the parallel case where both killings were intentional and both heirs pardoned, leaving half to the owner. Here, the accidental heir's right remains over the whole, so the division is based on proportions: accidental heir has 10,000 rights, intentional heir has 5,000, so 2:1 ratio. The commentary notes this is a dispute of 'awl (proportional reduction) and munaza'ah (dispute).

Key Terms
عمد (amad): Intentional killing or injury.
خطأ (khata'): Accidental killing or injury, only diyah (blood-money) is due.
عول (awl): Proportional reduction of shares when the total exceeds the estate.
منازعة (munaza'ah): Dispute or contest over shares, leading to proportional division.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the case where one slave kills intentionally and the other accidentally, and one of the intentional heirs pardons, what is the division of the slave according to Abu Hanifa?
A) The accidental heir gets half, the non-pardoning intentional heir gets half.
B) The accidental heir gets two-thirds, the non-pardoning intentional heir gets one-third.
C) The accidental heir gets three-quarters, the non-pardoning intentional heir gets one-quarter.
D) The slave is set free and no blood-money is paid.

Key Takeaway
In an intra-Hanafi dispute, the principle of 'awl is applied differently: Abu Hanifa uses direct ratio of claims, while the Sahibayn use staged division; the relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's.
